  119. I will preface my review by a description of my hair: very, very long (to my hips) with natural spiral curls (Type 3A/B, for those who care). While it may sound bizarre for a person like me to want to use hot rollers in their naturally curly hair, I do have a logical reason. Using hot rollers changes my curl pattern from a long spiral-type curl to more of a big, bouncy and looser curl. Although I do enjoy wearing my hair in its natural state, sometimes I want large &#34;glamorous&#34; curls instead. These Remington Ceramic rollers give me exactly the kinds of curls I've been hoping for! Since I do have quite a bit of hair, I knew that one set of these rollers would not be enough. I saw them at Target, and purchased the only two sets in stock, and for basically the same price as Amazon.<br /><br />There are three reasons I purchased these hot rollers:<br />1. They are ceramic rollers WITHOUT the velvet flocking that so many rollers seem to have. My hair does not hold curl when I use flocked rollers. Flocking also seems to act like Velcro to my hair, whereby the smooth-surface rollers like these are much easier to remove without tangling my very long hair.<br />2. These rollers come with the U-shaped wire pins instead of those dreadful butterfly clips. The wire pins never crease my hair, whereas butterfly clips inevitably do.<br />3. The set is compact and portable for travel, and the soft case has pockets for storing the wire pins. I'm amazed at how many hot roller sets on the market no longer provide storage for their corresponding clips or pins.<br /><br />As for the rollers, there are ten in a set. The five larger rollers are 1.25&#34; in diameter, and the five smaller rollers are 1&#34; in diameter. I find it best to allow the rollers to heat for approximately 5 minutes minimum, despite the manufacturer suggestion of 90 seconds. Before using the rollers, I wash my hair and allow it to dry naturally, while occasionally brushing it to discourage my own natural curls from forming. Once my hair is completely dry, I apply a heat-protectant spray, brush through, then a light coating of an anti-humidity hairspray. Around my face and on the crown of my head, I use all of the smaller rollers from both sets I purchased. For the remainder of my hair on the sides and back, I use all of the larger rollers from both sets. The ends of the rollers are perfectly comfortable to the touch, and I never burn my fingertips like some rollers can cause. I've had no difficulty with the wire pins, and they slide into position nicely, holding the rollers exactly where I place them. Once the rollers are in place, all twenty of them from the two sets I bought, they are quite heavy. Most people will use only one set, so the weight should not be an issue. Allowing for cooling time, I've been leaving the rollers in position for around 25-30 minutes, but again, I do have a lot of very long hair. After the rollers have cooled, I begin unwinding. These curlers do not get tangled in my hair, and the resulting curls are nicely formed. I find it best to wait a couple of minutes after removing all the rollers before I start touching my curls. I then spray with another mist of anti-humidity hairspray, bend forward at the waist, and lightly tousle my hair at the scalp. The curls loosen up a bit, and I'm left with healthy-looking hair that requires no further styling. The curls last into the next day! I hope you will love these hot rollers as much as I do. They have taken the place of my previous sets.own natural curls from forming. I have thick, shoulder-length, naturally curly hair (type 3a) but find I often need a more tame/professional look at work, and these do the trick (and also require MUCH less product to keep my hair looking nice, which is a huge benefit when traveling). I use the larger rollers at the crown of my head, and the smaller ones on the shorter hair at the side and in the back; for the small rollers, I put more hair in them so the curls don't end up like ringlets. I leave them in a few minutes, then spritz with a bit of hairspray after I take them out, and am ready to go. If any sections of hair come out too ringlet-like, I'll tug the curl out a bit before spraying. I end up with large wavy frizz-free curls that are manageable, soft, and hold all day. If I'm at home or getting ready for a non-work occasion, I'll often leave in a bit longer to get tighter curls. Finally - I know one of the most important feature in a hot roller is how well it stays secured in your hair, and that can differ significantly based on hair type; these work phenomenally for me (the combination of the rubberized texture of the roller, and the type of pin included). I'm not sure how well they would work for people with thin/fine hair, although I also used them once on a friend who has very fine/thin hair, and they worked well on her too.

  663. I purchased this set to replace a set of old wax core rollers I had, which came in a large, hard plastic case that had bare metal rods on which to heat them, and plastic clips that had to be stored separately from the rollers.<br /><br />When I received these, I was pleasantly surprised by how compact they are. They're meant to be heated inside the case, which has two small front pockets to hold the clips (I removed the clips before I got started, since I wasn't sure how hot they'd get next to the rollers). They claim to be &#34;instant heat&#34; and the instruction booklet says they're hot enough to create a wavy effect within 90 seconds, although you can allow them to heat to the full temperature for tighter curls. It doesn't specify how long it takes them to reach that point, so I left them for 10 minutes while I did some other things.<br /><br />The rollers were easy to handle, and the rubbery texture kept them from sliding too much through my hair. I used all 5 of the larger size and 3 of the smaller for my test run. I was worried that the metal pins would be hard to use, but I found the hold was actually much better than that of the plastic claw clips I was used to.<br /><br />I have shoulder-length, very straight, fine, and color-treated (lightened) hair, which is hard to curl. These hot rollers made a tight curl in my hair in just 20 minutes from start to finish (when they cooled and I removed them), which was easy for me to finger comb and rearrange into the looser look that I wanted. I think I could easily use all 10 for fuller body and a more evenly distributed style.<br /><br />There would likely not be enough rollers in this set for anyone with longer hair, or thicker hair, than my own, although they heat quickly enough that I think anyone with long/thick hair could easily do half, put them back into the case to reheat, and do the other side without too much fuss. This went much faster (for me) than using any other kind of hair appliance, and I suppose if you wanted to save time, they're cost effective enough that you could purchase two sets.<br /><br />I'm very satisfied with these, and the compact size should be very easy to travel with; at around 6&#34; long, this case will probably take up less space in my suitcase than a single shoe. I was reluctant for years to try hot rollers because I was figured they'd be a waste of money. Curling irons never get a curl into my hair, ever. Even when I go to a pro, they struggle to get a curl into my hair. After seeing so many people recommend hot rollers especially for hair that's like mine, I decided to take a chance with hot rollers and decided to try this set since it's smaller and not as pricey as others on the market.<br /><br />From the picture and description, I thought that I'd need two sets to work all my hair into the rollers and I can actually get away with one set if I want looser curls. This look is good for everyday. I might need the second set for more tight curls. For reference, my hair is layered and the longest layer reaches the small of my back. I have lots of fine hair, as well. Like I said, I never had much success with anything else that's supposed to curl your hair but, with these, not only are they fast and easy, they curl my hair without an issue.<br /><br />HEAT: They heat up at a decent rate. I think they reach optimum temp. in about 3 minutes, unlike the description states. This isn't an issue for me but, if you were looking for something that heats up much quicker than that, these might be a disappointment to you. They hold their heat well while they are in your hair. Also, I don't have an issue where some curlers heat up and others don't like other people stated in their reviews but, to be safe, I always make sure that they are pushed all the way into the heating device while heating up.<br /><br />CLIPS: They come with their own clips. They are the metal kind and I've heard that these kind are the best since they don't leave marks or creases in your hair. I also, unlike other reviewers, didn't have an issue with these clips and their holdability. They stay put and don't flop around. I think that if you're having this issue, you might be putting too much hair around one roller. I can't be certain of that but, that's what I suspect.<br /><br />SIZE: These are definitely a portable set and if you plan to use these as a travel set, they are extremely compact. I like that they are compact because, unlike other sets, they don't have bulky cases that would take up far too much space in my bathroom. Even with my two sets, I feel like they're the perfect size and don't take up much space at all.<br /><br />Overall, I love these and I'd recommend them to everyone looking to purchase some hot rollers.

  743. YES they will curl your hair, (though I am sure there are a few exceptions). The case is very small and compact, although the image here makes the case look much larger. I have not purchased curlers in a long time, so I found it odd that the nylon case the curlers are in, has a cord coming out of it that plugs into the wall...but maybe I am just out of the loop in the world of curlers.<br /><br />TIP: I think curlers went out of style a while back, (though they never should have because they are much less of a hassle than the curling iron) so for those of you who are not familiar, here are some basic tips.<br />1. Plug them up and let them heat for 15-20 minutes.<br />2. Don't straighten your hair before hand (even if you have bad frizz like me) because it makes it harder to re-curl. If you need to straighten some parts, do it afterward.<br />3. If you like, you can spritz your hair with some styling/heating formula<br />4. Roll your hair. You may have to try this a few different times before you get your desired results. Some people like to roll the hair under, some over, some all the way up to the root, some not, some like to use just the big curlers, ect. If the roller is hot on your neck, tuck some tissue or TP between the roller and your neck.<br />5. WAIT UNTIL CURLERS FEEL MOSTLY COOL ON YOUR HEAD. This is key! When they are cool, take the rollers out. If you feel the curls are too tight, run your fingers through your hair/flip your head over/brush it. If it looks just right, spritz it with hairspray, let it set for 5 min, and then run your fingers through your hair/flip your head over/brush it. After that, spray again.
